# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

53-assistanttext-
I have successfully traced the Kafka consumer offset commit flow and created a comprehensive answer document. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Kafka Consumer Offset Commit Flow

The flow travels through the following key components:

**Client Side (Consumer):**
1. `KafkaConsumer.commitSync()` - Public API entry point
2. `ClassicKafkaConsumer.commitSync()` - Implementation that delegates to coordinator
3. `ConsumerCoordinator.commitOffsetsSync()` - Synchronous commit with retry logic
4. `ConsumerCoordinator.sendOffsetCommitRequest()` - Constructs and sends the OffsetCommitRequest

**Broker Side (Group Coordinator):**
5. `KafkaApis.handleOffsetCommitRequest()` - Receives request, validates authorization
6. `GroupCoordinatorService.commitOffsets()` - Schedules the write operation
7. `GroupCoordinatorShard.commitOffset()` - Shard-level handler
8. `OffsetMetadataManager.commitOffset()` - Creates offset commit records
9. `GroupCoordinatorRecordHelpers.newOffsetCommitRecord()` - Creates the CoordinatorRecord with OffsetCommitKey/Value

**Log Append:**
The records are appended to the `__consumer_offsets` topic via the coordinator runtime, ensuring persistence across replicas before returning success.

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, the call chain, and a detailed narrative explanation of the entire flow.

!ensureCoordinatorReadyAsync();\n495:     }\n496: \n497:     /**\n498:      * Poll for coordinator events. This ensures that the coordinator is known and that the consumer\n499:      * has joined the group (if it is using group management). This also handles periodic offset commits\n500:      * if they are enabled.\n501:      * <p>\n502:      * Returns early if the timeout expires or if waiting on rejoin is not required\n503:      *\n504:      * @param timer Timer bounding how long this method can block\n505:      * @param waitForJoinGroup Boolean flag indicating if we should wait until re-join group completes\n506:      * @throws KafkaException if the rebalance callback throws an exception\n507:      * @return true iff the operation succeeded\n508:      */\n509:     public boolean poll(Timer timer, boolean waitForJoinGroup) {\n510:         maybeUpdateSubscriptionMetadata();\n511: \n512:         invokeCompletedOffsetCommitCallbacks();\n513: \n514:         if (subscriptions.hasAutoAssignedPartitions()) {\n515:             if (protocol == null) {\n516:                 throw new IllegalStateException(\"User configured \" + ConsumerConfig.PARTITION_ASSIGNMENT_STRATEGY_CONFIG +\n517:                     \" to empty while trying to subscribe for group protocol to auto assign partitions\");\n518:             }\n519:             // Always update the heartbeat last poll time so that the heartbeat thread does not leave the\n520:             // group proactively due to application inactivity even if (say) the coordinator cannot be found.\n521:             pollHeartbeat(timer.currentTimeMs());\n522:             if (coordinatorUnknownAndUnreadySync(timer)) {\n523:                 return false;\n524:             }\n525: \n526:             if (rejoinNeededOrPending()) {\n527:                 // due to a race condition between the initial metadata fetch and the initial rebalance,\n528:                 // we need to ensure that the metadata is fresh before joining initially. This ensures\n529:                 // that we have matched the pattern against the cluster's topics at least once before joining.\n530:                 if (subscriptions.hasPatternSubscription()) {\n531:                     // For consumer group that uses pattern-based subscription, after a topic is created,\n532:                     // any consumer that discovers the topic after metadata refresh can trigger rebalance\n533:                     // across the entire consumer group. Multiple rebalances can be triggered after one topic\n534:                     // creation if consumers refresh metadata at vastly different times. We can significantly\n535:                     // reduce the number of rebalances caused by single topic creation by asking consumer to\n536:                     // refresh metadata before re-joining the group as long as the refresh backoff time has\n537:                     // passed.\n538:                     if (this.metadata.timeToAllowUpdate(timer.currentTimeMs()) == 0) {\n539:                         this.metadata.requestUpdate(true);\n540:                     }\n541: \n542:                     if (!client.ensureFreshMetadata(timer)) {\n543:                         return false;\n544:                     }\n545: \n546:                     maybeUpdateSubscriptionMetadata();\n547:                 }\n548: \n549:                 // if not wait for join group, we would just use a timer of 0\n550:                 if (!ensureActiveGroup(waitForJoinGroup ? timer : time.timer(0L))) {\n551:                     // since we may use a different timer in the callee, we'd still need\n552:                     // to update the original timer's current time after the call\n553:                     timer.update(time.milliseconds());\n554: \n555:                     return false;\n556:                 }\n557:             }\n558:         } else {\n559:             // For manually assigned partitions, we do not try to pro-actively lookup coordinator;\n560:             // instead we only try to refresh metadata when necessary.\n561:             // If connections to all nodes fail, wakeups triggered while attempting to send fetch\n562:             // requests result in polls returning immediately, causing a tight loop of polls. Without\n563:             // the wakeup, poll() with no channels would block for the timeout, delaying re-connection.\n564:             // awaitMetadataUpdate() in ensureCoordinatorReady initiates new client.awaitMetadataUpdate(timer);\n567:             }\n568: \n569:             // if there is pending coordinator requests, ensure they have a chance to be transmitted.\n570:             client.pollNoWakeup();\n571:         }\n572: \n573:         maybeAutoCommitOffsetsAsync(timer.currentTimeMs());\n574:         return true;\n575:     }\n576: \n577:     /**\n578:      * Return the time                      final Map<String, Assignment> assignments) {\n724:         Set<TopicPartition> totalRevokedPartitions = new HashSet<>();\n725:         SortedSet<TopicPartition> private void maybeMarkPartitionsPendingRevocation() {\n865:         if (protocol != RebalanceProtocol.EAGER) {\n866:             return;\n867:         }\n868: \n869:         // When asynchronously It is\n871:         // possible for pending fetches for these partitions to return during this time, which means the application's\n872:         // position may get ahead of the committed position prior to revocation. This can cause duplicate consumption.\n873:         // To prevent this, we mark the partitions as \"pending revocation,\" which stops the Fetcher from sending new\n874:         // fetches or returning {}\", partitions);\n877:         subscriptions.markPendingRevocation(partitions);\n878:     }\n879: \n880:     @Override\n881:     public void onLeavePrepare() {\n882:         // Save the current @Override\n913:     public boolean rejoinNeededOrPending() {\n914:         if (!subscriptions.hasAutoAssignedPartitions())\n915:             return false;\n916: \n917:         // we need to rejoin if \n937:     /**\n938:      * Refresh the committed offsets for partitions that require initialization.\n939:      *\n940:      * @param timer Timer bounding how long this method can block\n941:      * callback) {\n1047:         invokeCompletedOffsetCommitCallbacks();\n1048: \n1049:         RequestFuture<Void> future = null;\n1050:         if (offsets.isEmpty()) {\n1051:             // No need to check coordinator if offsets is empty since commit of empty offsets is completed locally.\n1052:             future = doCommitOffsetsAsync(offsets, callback);\n1053:         } else if (!coordinatorUnknownAndUnreadyAsync()) {\n1054:             // we need to make sure coordinator is ready before committing, since\n1055:             // this is for async committing we do not try to block, but just try once to\n1056:             // clear the previous discover-coordinator future, resend, or get responses;\n1057:             // if the coordinator is not ready yet then we would just proceed and put that into the\n1058:             // pending requests, and future poll calls would still try to complete them.\n1059:             //\n1060:             // the key here though is that we ConsumerCoordinator.commitOffsetsSync()\\nCore synchronous commit logic at `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java:1140-1176`. This method:\\n- Invokes pending offset commit callbacks\\n- Calls `sendOffsetCommitRequest()` to send the actual request to the coordinator\\n- Polls the client until the response is received or timeout occurs\\n- Throws CommitFailedException or RebalanceInProgressException on unrecoverable errors\\n\\n### 4. ConsumerCoordinator.sendOffsetCommitRequest()\\nImplementation at `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/ConsumerCoordinator.java:1270-1343`. The actual log append is handled by:\\n- `CoordinatorRuntime.scheduleWriteOperation()` which manages the write to the underlying Kafka log\\n- The records are written to the __consumer_offsets topic partition that corresponds to the group's partition (calculated via hash of groupId)\\n- The operation ensures all in-sync replicas acknowledge the write before returning success to the client\\n\\n## Summary\\n\\nThe flow creates a chain of responsibility from the consumer application to the persistent __consumer_offsets topic:\\n1. Consumer calls commitSync() on KafkaConsumer\\n2. Request is routed through ClassicKafkaConsumer -> ConsumerCoordinator\\n3. OffsetCommitRequest is sent to the group coordinator broker\\n4. Broker validates and routes through KafkaApis -> GroupCoordinatorService\\n5. Coordinator shard processes via OffsetMetadataManager\\n6. Offset commit records are created and appended to __consumer_offsets log\\n7. Response is sent back to client confirming persistence across replicas\"\n}\n",

Broker validates and routes through KafkaApis -> GroupCoordinatorService\\n5. Coordinator shard processes via OffsetMetadataManager\\n6. Offset commit records are created and appended to __consumer_offsets log\\n7. Response is sent back to client confirming persistence across replicas\"\n}\n",
  "filePath": "/workspace/answer.json",
